<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper deals with a low-cost method for the assembly of flexible substrate antennas and UHF RF identification silicon (Si) chips. Such a method exploits a magnetic coupling mechanism, thus not requiring for galvanic contacts between the Si chip and antenna itself. The magnetic coupling is established by a planar transformer, the primary and secondary windings of which are implemented on flexible substrate and Si chip, respectively. As a result, the Si chip can be assembled on the antenna with a mere placing and gluing process. First, the idea has been validated by theory. Electromagnetic simulations of a square heterogeneous transformer (1.0-mm side) show a maximum available power gain (MAG) of -0.4 dB at 868 MHz. In addition, the heterogeneous transformer is also quite tolerant with respect to misalignment between primary and secondary. An offset error of 150 Î¼m reduces the MAG to - 0.5 dB. A sub-optimal matching strategy, exploiting a simple on-chip capacitor, is then developed for antennas with 50- Î© input impedances. Finally, the idea has been experimentally validated exploiting printed circuit board (PCB) prototypes. A PCB transformer (1.5-mm side) and a transformer rectifier (two-diode Dickson multiplier) have been fabricated and tested. Measurements indicates a MAG of -0.3 dB at 868 MHz for the transformer and the capability of the developed rectifier to supply a 220-kÎ© load at 1.5 V with a - 2-dBm input power.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF identification (RFID) tags working in the UHF frequency range rely on ultra-low power CMOS circuits and flexible substrate antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. Today, the typical cost of these tags is around $0.1, most of this amount being associated to the assembly of the CMOS die on the flexible substrate. Among several mounting processes, the most effective one <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a> is based on fluidic self assembly (FSA). With FSA, specifically shaped semiconductor devices are suspended in liquid and flowed over a surface that has correspondingly shaped holes or receptors on it and into which the devices settle. The shapes of the devices and holes are designed so that the devices are easily self aligned into place. FSA is typically divided in six process steps, the last one being devoted to the electrical connection of the assembled CMOS chip via standard metallization techniques. Since the pads on the CMOS chips are relatively small in diameter (80 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.68em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or less), an accurate alignment is required.</p><p>In this paper, the possibility of completely avoiding the last FSA step (i.e., the electrical connection step) is considered. To this purpose, the CMOS chip is magnetically coupled to the antenna realized on the flexible substrate, thus eliminating all the galvanic contacts between the chip and the antenna itself <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. The magnetic coupling is established, as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, by a heterogeneous planar transformer, the primary and secondary windings of which are implemented on flexible (paper) substrate and Si chip, respectively. As a result, the RFID chip can be mounted on the flexible substrate by mere placing and gluing process steps. In particular, the chip will be padless and completely passivated, the pad-ring being substituted by the secondary coil (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-10" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.48em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-family: MathJax_SansSerif;">S</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\ssr S</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>) of the transformer.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>RFID chip (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-13" role="math" style="width: 0.665em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.532em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.458em 1000.47em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-17"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-18"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_SansSerif;">C</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.838em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">{\scriptstyle\ssr C}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is magnetically coupled to the antenna (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-20" role="math" style="width: 0.665em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.532em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1000.53em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-21"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-25"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-26" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_SansSerif;">A</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.754em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">{\scriptstyle\ssr A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). Such a coupling is obtained by a transformer, the primary (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-27" role="math" style="width: 0.665em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.532em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1000.47em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-28"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-31"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-32"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-33" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_SansSerif;">P</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.754em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">{\scriptstyle\ssr P}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and secondary (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-34" role="math" style="width: 0.599em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.466em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.458em 1000.4em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-35"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-36"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-37"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-38"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-40" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_SansSerif;">S</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.838em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">{\scriptstyle\ssr S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) windings of which are fabricated on the antenna (paper) substrate and Si chip, respectively. In this way, the need for galvanic connection between antenna and chip is avoided. After <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The first and more evident advantage of the novel design solution is the possibility to further reduce mounting costs by cutting one step of the FSA process. The second advantage is related to the market exploitation of flexible antennas on paper substrates <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. These antennas can be fabricated by direct ink-jet printing, and thus, are well suited for ultra-low-cost RFID tags. The mounting of CMOS chips, however, has been never experimented, mainly because of the difficulty of establishing an electrical connection between the chip pads and the metal lines on paper substrate. That is exactly what the proposed solution eliminates.</p><p>Flexible electronics, in fact, is facing a significant growth in terms of scientific attention and industrial investments due to the continuous request for light weight, shape adaptability, space saving, and economical, as well as environmental friendly electronics <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. This is leading the research toward the use of innovative technologies such as ink-jet printing on unusual substrates such as paper. Paper is recently showing to be more than a simple candidate for flexible RF electronics <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>: it is a low-cost substrate since it is organic, and thus, universally available; it is well suited for reel-to-reel manufacturing and mass production. The ink-jet printing allows avoiding the commonly used etching process and it is a faster and cheaper technology with respect to the classical printed circuit board (PCB) manufacturing process (no photo-lithographic mask fabrication). Today, the most important fields of application of this innovative approach are RFIDs, wireless sensors, and flexible electronics <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>. RFID tag planar antenna design has been already exploited as proof of the goodness of such a technological trend <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>.</p><p>A first experiment of a tag antenna magnetically coupled to an RFID chip has been demonstrated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, a UHF RFID tag has been realized on a standard 0.18-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-41" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-43" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-44"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-46"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-47"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-48" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS, including an on-chip loop antenna. In this paper, the two above ideas are further expanded. In particular, a multiturn primary winding is proposed in order to increase the coupling factor and to reduce the insertion losses. A further insertion loss reduction has been obtained by placing primary and secondary windings face-to-face. The heterogeneous transformer has been studied by means of electromagnetic simulations and the optimal solution to the matching problem is illustrated. An equivalent circuit is given and this can be used by the interested readers to test the impact of the magnetic coupling technique with already developed RFID tag designs. The placing errors in gluing the Si chip (with the secondary winding) on the paper substrate (with the primary winding) have been analyzed. Finally, the matching of a paper-antenna prototype has been studied and the experimental results have been obtained showing a transformer-coupled two-stage Dickson rectifier.</p><p>For the success of the proposed approach, two questions must be answered. The first question is related to the losses of heterogeneous transformer. The minimum losses are given by the maximum available gain (MAG) of the transformer itself, as suggested in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>, and can be achieved in simultaneous matching conditions. The second question concerns the interferences between the transformer magnetic field and the CMOS electronics. Such a point is particularly important when all the RFID tag circuitry is within the secondary winding of the transformer. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a>, however, it has been demonstrated that the above interference is negligible and that the âcircuit-in-the-coilâ approach is feasible.</p><p>This paper is organized as follows. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, a paper to Si heterogeneous transformer is studied by means of electromagnetic numerical simulations. The MAG of such a transformer is taken as the main figure-of-merit and an equivalent circuit is derived. The effect of alignment errors is also considered in this section. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> is devoted to the matching between the antenna and RFID chip. Starting from a fabricated and measured paper antenna prototype, both optimal and conventional strategies will be investigated. Finally, in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>, experimental results are presented. A PCB transformer and transformerârectifier prototypes have been fabricated and measured to verify the feasibility of the idea and the accuracy of the design flow.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Coupling Transformer</h2></div><p>The proposed idea has first been validated by electromagnetic simulations. To this purpose, an heterogeneous transformer between the paper substrate and CMOS Si chip is studied. The geometry of such a transformer has been defined on the basis of the following constraints. On the paper substrate, the primary winding is assumed to be printed exploiting an ink-jet technology. The minimum metal track width and spacing are 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-49" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-50"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-51" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-52"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-53"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-54"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-55"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, corresponding to the maximum spatial resolution of the ink-jet printer. On silicon, a typical RFID chip size of 1 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-57" role="math" style="width: 2.345em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.144em 1002.11em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-58"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-59"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-60"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-61"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-62"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-63"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-64" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-65"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-66"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-67" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">{\hbox {mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is considered. The secondary windings is substantially that reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2">[12]</a>. Such a winding could be substituted to the pad-ring of the chip and all the required tag electronics fabricated inside this coil. Further considerations on the heterogeneous transformer design are reported in <a ref-type="app" anchor="app1" class="fulltext-link">Appendix A</a>.</p><p>The complete parameter set is quoted in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. Primary and secondary windings have been placed face-to-face, as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>, and separated by a distance of 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-68" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-69"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-70" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-71"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-72"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-73"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-74"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-75" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The spacing layer has been assumed filled of air <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-76" role="math" style="width: 3.907em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.486em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.37em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-77"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-78" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-79"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-80" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Îµ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-81"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-82"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-83" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-84" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-85" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-86" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">(\varepsilon_{r}=1)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For the secondary coil, a 0.25-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-87" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-88"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-89" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-90"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-91"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-92"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-93"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-94" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> SiGe BiCMOS process has been taken into account. This process allows for five metal layers. The last two metal layers (top layers) are characterized by thick traces (i.e., 2 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-95" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-96"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-97" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-98"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-99"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-100"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-101"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-102" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for M4 and 3 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-103" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-104"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-105" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-106"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-107"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-108"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-109"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-110" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for M5), particularly suited for the fabrication of spiral inductors and transformers. The secondary winding has been implemented on M5.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Geometrical Parameters of Paper to Si Transformer<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Simulated heterogeneous transformer and zoomed cross section of the metal line geometry. Primary and secondary windings are designed to maximize the interfaced area under the given constraints.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The above structure has been numerically analyzed by means of a full-wave electromagnetic simulator. The obtained results are reported in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> where the maximum available power gain (MAG) of the transformer is plotted. This figure-of-merit has already been used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a> to characterize the coupling performances of integrated transformers. As can be seen form this figure, the MAG of the basic structure is â0.4 dB at 868 MHz, thus indicating that, with the right matching, only 8.8% of the incident power is lost inside the transformer (or, alternatively, 91.2% of the power is transferred from primary to secondary). The self resonance frequency of the structure is at about 3.5 GHz.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>MAG of the paper-substrate to Si chip transformer without and with alignment offset error between primary and secondary. The offset error is equal to 150 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-111" role="math" style="width: 1.789em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.392em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.591em 1001.39em 2.649em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-112"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-113" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-114"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-115"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-116"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-117"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The data obtained by electromagnetic simulations are compared to the MAG of the extracted transformer equivalent circuit.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Now consider the case where a silver conductive ink is adopted for the printing of the primary winding. In this case, some of the parameters reported in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> need to be adjusted. The silver ink conductivity, for example, is around 25 MS/m, as stated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a>. The ink thickness, instead, is around 2 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-119" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-121" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-122"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-123"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-124"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-125"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-126" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as pointed-out by <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2">[15]</a>. Repeating the above simulations with these values, only a minor degradation of the transformer MAG is observed, namely, from â0.4 to â0.5 dB at 868 MHz.</p><p>A second study that has been carried out is related to the effect of placing errors. These errors can arise when the RFID chip (carrying the secondary winding) is aligned with the antenna substrate (carrying the primary winding). At this point, it is important to recall that the FSA process is specified for an alignment error less than 1 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-127" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-128"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-129" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-130"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-132"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-134" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and that bonding pads in CMOS chips do not have a diameter greater than 80 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-135" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-136"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-137" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-138"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-139"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-140"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In the proposed numerical experiment, an offset error as large as 150 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-143" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-144"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-145" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-146"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-147"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-148"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-149"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-150" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is considered. With such an error, a galvanic contact down to 80-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-151" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-152"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-153" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-154"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-155"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-156"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-157"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-158" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> pads is no more feasible. With such an offset error, the MAG of the transformer is equal to â0.5 dB at 868 MHz, i.e., only â0.1 dB worse than that with perfect alignment (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>). This means that the proposed innovation allows for automatic antenna-to-RFID assembly by standard pick-and-place machines, the latter being typically specified for a placing error of about 100 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-159" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-160"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-161" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-163"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-164"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-165"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-166" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Another parameter that has been considered during this study is the side length of the secondary (Si) winding. The RFID chip, in fact, has the trend of shrinking the size due to the continuous scaling of microelectronic technologies. As a consequence, the proposed magnetic coupling approach could have some limitations for very small RFID chips (i.e., secondary winding of small size). The size of the primary winding has been kept constant because this is mainly related to the resolution of the ink-jet printing process (see <a ref-type="app" anchor="app1" class="fulltext-link">Appendix A</a>). The results of such an analysis are reported in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>. From the figure, it emerges that the transformer with the smallest secondary winding (390 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-167" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-168"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-169" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-170"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-171"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-172"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-173"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-174" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> side) has a MAG of about â1 dB at 868 MHz. This value is only 0.6 dB worse than that of the typical case (790 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-175" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-176"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-177" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-178"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-179"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-180"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-181"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-182" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> side) in spite of a four times reduction of the active area.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>MAG of the paper-substrate to Si chip transformer for different side lengths of the secondary (Si) winding. The size of the primary winding has been kept constant to the value of <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Finally, the electromagnetic simulation results have been used to determine the parameters of a transformer equivalent circuit, according to the scheme of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. This equivalent circuit has used by several authors to model Si integrated transformers <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_2">[16]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_2">[17]</a> and is available under Agilent ADS. The losses on the two substrates (displacement current on paper, displacement and eddy currents on Si) are modeled by the single resistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-183" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-184"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-185"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-186" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-187"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-188"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-189" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">p</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">R_{p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The equivalent circuit is derived in the frequency range from 300 MHz to 2 GHz (see <a ref-type="app" anchor="app2" class="fulltext-link">Appendix B</a>). The MAG of the extracted equivalent circuit is plotted again in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> and is in good agreement with the electromagnetic simulations.

<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Antenna to RFID Chip Matching</h2></div><p>This section is devoted to the problem of the maximum power transfer between antenna and RFID chip, when the heterogeneous (paper-to-Si) transformer is exploited. As it is well known, passive, i.e., batteryless RFID tags, rely on the energy directly scavenged from the incoming RF carrier provided by the reader. Such an RF energy is rectified and used to supply all the tag electronics. Maximizing the power transfer through the heterogeneous transformer is thus a key design point to improve activation distance performances.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Simultaneous Conjugate Matching</h3><p>For a lossy passive two-port network (which is a stable network by definition), it is always possible to find a pair of optimum source and load impedances, namely, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-309" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; padding-left: 0.202em;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-381" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.202em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-382" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">89</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-383" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-384" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.496em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.754em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">Z_{L}^{\rm opt}=90-j89\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. After <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_3a">[4]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>From a design point of view, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> indicates the optimum solution to the maximum power transfer problem. This means that, in order to let the transformer working in the best conditions as possible, the input impedances of both antenna and RFID circuit must be designed to meet <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-385" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.084em 1001.87em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-386"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-387"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-388" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.08em 4.327em -999.997em); top: -4.502em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-389"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-390"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-391" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-392" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-393" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.661em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-394"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-395"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-396" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.463em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.537em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">Z_{S}^{\rm opt}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-397" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.084em 1001.87em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-398"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-399"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-400" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.08em 4.327em -999.997em); top: -4.502em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-401"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-402"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-403" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-404" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-405" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.721em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-406"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-407"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-408" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.537em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">Z_{L}^{\rm opt}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively, thus allowing the power transfer ratio from the antenna to the RFID circuit to achieve the MAG level of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>.</p><p>The above optimum terminations require a significant capacitive component, mainly because of the inductive nature of the transformer. The dipole antenna can easily be capacitively tuned working on its length (slightly shorter than the resonance length). The RFID circuit input impedance, instead, is mainly associated to that of its input stage, i.e., the rectifier stage. Such an impedance is naturally capacitive and can be tuned to the right value by means of a simple on-chip capacitor.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Paper Substrate Antennas</h3><p>Antennas on paper substrates have recently been developed for ultra-low-cost UHF RFID applications <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_3b">[18]</a>. These substrates are flexible, inexpensive, and characterized by a relatively good dielectric properties <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_3b">[5]</a>. In addition, ink-jet metal printing on paper was chosen as potentially capable of reel-to-reel manufacturing and mass production.</p><p>To further reduce costs, the well-known bow-tie antenna shape <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_3b">[19]</a> has been modified in order to optimize the amount of silver ink used. In particular portions of solid printed surfaces have been removed, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>. A detailed study of such a design approach has been reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_3b">[20]</a> and will not be repeated here. This design is based on the current distribution of the bow-tie antenna. The highest concentration mainly occurs close to the center of the radiating body, and thus the related portion of metal is not removed. The simulated radiation gain is equal to 1.7 dBi.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Fabricated UHF bow-tie antenna on paper substrate. padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-424" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">27</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-425" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-426"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-427"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-428"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-429"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-430" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; <p></p><p>The measurements have been performed using groundâsignal (GS) probe tips with 1-mm pitch. The fabricated antenna was placed on a custom-made probe station (exploiting high density polystyrene foam with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-431" role="math" style="width: 4.447em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-435"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-436"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-437" style="font-size: 70.7%; The input reflection coefficient of the paper-substrate bow-tie antenna is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. The experimental data are in good agreement with electromagnetic simulations. The antenna exhibits a 7% bandwidth covering the European UHF RFID frequency range.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Return loss of the fabricated bow-tie antenna: comparison between measurements and simulations. <p></p><p>Finally, the bow-tie antenna input impedance has been approximated, in the considered frequency range, by the equivalent circuit shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>. This equivalent circuit is constituted by a series resonator <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-443" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; vertical-align: -2.73em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 5.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-55">\eqalignno{\omega_{b}=&amp;\,{1\over\sqrt{L_{b}C_{b}}}&amp;\hbox{(2)}\cr Q_{b}=&amp;\,{\omega_{b}L_{b}\over R_{b}}={1\over\omega_{b}C_{b}R_{b}}.&amp;\hbox{(3)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{\omega_{b}=&amp;\,{1\over\sqrt{L_{b}C_{b}}}&amp;\hbox{(2)}\cr Q_{b}=&amp;\,{\omega_{b}L_{b}\over R_{b}}={1\over\omega_{b}C_{b}R_{b}}.&amp;\hbox{(3)}}</span></span></disp-formula>The equivalent-circuit parameters are quoted in the caption of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> and have been found by fitting <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> to the measurements of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. The agreement between the equivalent-circuit model and experiments is good, as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>.

<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>(a) Real and (b) imaginary parts of the bow-tie antenna input impedance versus the frequency. Comparison between measured data and equivalent-circuit model.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The bow-tie antenna of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> is a typical example of a UHF RFID antenna, pre-matched at an impedance level of 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-767" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-768"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-769" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. A capacitive tuning of this antenna can be obtained adjusting the length of the folded line and the size of the radiating elements.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Matching With On-Chip Capacitor</h3><p>A sub-optimal solution to the maximum power transfer problem can also be found when an antenna, pre-matched to a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-770" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-771"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-772" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> impedance level, is given. In that case, one can only tune the RFID input impedance to a proper value. This situation is summarized in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11(a)</a> where an on-chip capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-773" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-774"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-775"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-776" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-777"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-778"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-779" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">C_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is adopted as tuning element. As a first-order approximation, it will be assumed that the RFID chip input impedance is purely resistive and equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-780" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-781"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-782"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-783" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-784"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-785"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-786" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In practice, the impedance will mainly be determined by the rectifier circuit (as a function of frequency and input power) and it will have a capacitive value. In this study, such a capacitive value is embedded in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-787" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-788"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-789"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-790" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-791"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-792"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-793" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">C_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-794" role="math" style="width: 1.789em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.392em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.26em 1001.39em 2.517em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-795"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-796"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.392em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.731em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-798"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-799"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-800" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.246em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">C_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be used to optimize the power transfer between a pre-matched antenna (e.g., a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-801" role="math" style="width: 0.929em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.731em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.66em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-802"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-803" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px;
