(a). To evaluate the overall insertion loss, a circuit model is adopted. (b). In this model, the bow-tie antenna is represented through a Thevenin equivalent circuit. The chip (mainly the rectifier input impedance) is described by the resistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-804" role="math" style="width: 1.458em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.128em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.13em 2.517em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-805"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-806"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.128em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.73em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-807" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.731em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-808"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-809"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-810" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.246em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In order to evaluate the overall power transfer and to optimize it, the previously described bow-tie antenna is considered. This is a good example of pre-matched antenna with a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-811" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-812"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-813" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> impedance level at the frequency of 868 MHz. This study has been carried-out exploiting a Thevenin equivalent circuit for the bow-tie antenna in receiving mode, as depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11(b)</a>. The Thevenin equivalent impedance is derived from the antenna measurements in transmitting mode and it has already been defined in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>. The open-circuit voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-814" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; For <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-963" role="math" style="width: 5.529em; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">R_{c}=350\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the overall power transfer is â1.5 dB (i.e., about 70%), a quite good value even for the suboptimal solution proposed. This resistance level can be tuned, during the design, by adjusting the number of stages of the voltage multiplier and the rectifier diode area <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_3c">[21]</a>. In addition, part of the capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-974" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-975"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-976"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-977" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-978"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-979"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-980" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">C_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is embedded in the rectifier input impedance.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Overall power transfer between bow-tie antenna and chip for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-981" role="math" style="width: 6.617em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.228em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1005.16em 2.649em -999.997em); height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.246em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (mainly associated to the rectifier input resistance). For <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1003" role="math" style="width: 5.956em; <p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Experimental Results</h2></div><p>As a proof-of-the-concept, a planar transformer and a transformer-rectifier (two-diode Dickson voltage multiplier) prototypes have been realized exploiting a standard PCB technology on an RO4003 substrate material. The proposed experiment is consistent with the concept to be proven since the typical resolution today achievable with metal ink-jet printing on paper is similar to that of the considered PCB technologies. As a consequence, transformer structures of similar dimensions and electrical performances can be fabricated and tested. In addition, the via-hole connection necessary to the transformer layout can easily be fabricated exploiting such a PCB process. Similar via-hole connections, although not yet fully optimized for paper substrates, have already been fabricated <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_4">[22]</a>: the typical via-hole diameter is 200 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1014" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1015"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1016" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1017"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1018"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1019"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1020"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1021" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Transformer Results</h3><p>To emulate the Si chip to paper substrate magnetic coupling, the fixture of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a> has been developed. Such a fixture is composed by two separated PCBs each of them with a three-turn winding. The outer terminal of the windings is fed by a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1022" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1023"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1024" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> microstrip line, while the inner one, is connected to the microstrip ground. Such a ground connection is provided by a via-hole at the center of the winding and by a short metal track printed on the same layer of the microstrip ground [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13(b)</a>]. In this way, it is possible to remove the microstrip ground from the winding active area, thus resembling the groundless structure of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>Mechanical drawing of the: (a) PCB test-fixture and (b) zoom of its central zone with a highlight of the transformer structure. The tapering sections in (b) are used to connect the transformer to the feeding microstrips, whereas the two lateral bars are the related ground planes. From <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_4a">[4]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The geometrical parameters of the developed PCB transformer are quoted in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>. Primary and secondary windings have been placed face-to-face, as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13(a)</a>. In this case, the solder-resist film has been used to electrically isolate the two windings. The solder resist thickness is about 30 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1025" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1026"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1027" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1028"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1029"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1030"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1031"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1032" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, whereas its relative permittivity is equal to 4. The two PCBs are equal, thus giving a symmetrical transformer whose windings have a side of only 1.5 mm.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Geometrical Parameters of PCB Transformer<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table II" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>The fabricated test-fixture is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a>. In particular, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(a)</a> illustrates one of the two PCBs with the small winding covered by solder resist and fed by the microstrip line. The complete transformer structure is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(b)</a>, where a second PCB is added on top of the first one and kept in position by four plastic screws (i.e., no glue is used here).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14. </b><fig><p>Fabricated PCB test-fixture showing the: (a) primary winding alone and (b) the whole transformer. The latter has been obtained joining two equal planar windings in face-to-face configuration. From <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_4a">[4]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The structure of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a> has been experimentally characterized exploiting a vector network analyzer (VNA). The measured results are reported in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a> in a frequency range from dc to 1 GHz, i.e., including the RFID UHF 868- and 915-MHz bands. The discontinuities associated to both the SMA connector and to the feeding microstrip lines have been removed from measured data by means of a de-embedding procedure. This procedure is based on three steps. First, an open structure, i.e., a purposely designed calibration structure corresponding to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(a)</a> without the transformer coil, has been measured by the VNA. This open structure includes both the SMA adapter and feeding microstrip. A simple transmission line model of the open structure has then been assessed by fitting its computed <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1033" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1034"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1035"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1036" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1037"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1038"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1039" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">S_{11}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to that obtained by the calibration measurements. Finally, this transmission line model is used within a circuit simulator to extract the transformer scattering parameters.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 15. </b><fig><p>Scattering parameters of the PCB transformer prototype: comparison between measurements and simulations. These data are referred to a termination impedance of 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1040" role="math" style="width: 0.929em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.731em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.66em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1041"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1042" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at both ports. The MAG of this structure at 868 MHz is about â0.3 dB for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1043" role="math" style="width: 13.958em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 11.048em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.128em 1010.98em 2.781em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1044"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1045"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.855em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.73em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1046" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.31em 1001.13em 4.302em -999.997em); top: -4.428em; left: 0.797em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1047"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1048"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1049" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1050" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1051" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; <p></p><p>The measured data have been compared to the electromagnetic simulations of the isolated transformer. As can be seen from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a>, the overall agreement between measurements and simulations is good over the considered frequency range at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1073" role="math" style="width: 11.955em; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1084" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1085"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1086"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1087" style="font-size: 70.7%; This performance, however, is obtained in a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1098" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1099"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1100" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> measurement system. At the same frequency, the MAG (obtained from the measured scattering parameters) is much less and equal to only â0.3 dB. Due to symmetry, the simultaneous conjugate matching condition is given by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1101" role="math" style="width: 13.216em; Rectifier Results</h3><p>The second test structure that has been verified is a transformer, the secondary winding of which is connected to a rectifier. In particular, the two-diode Dickson voltage multiplier configuration of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16(a)</a> is adopted. The realized prototype is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16(b)</a> and it uses a matched pair of low-barrier Schottky diodes, i.e., the HSMS-2850 series device <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_4b">[23]</a>. The power transmitted from the secondary winding output to the rectifier input has been optimized by properly tuning the length of the uniform microstrip line placed between these two circuits.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 16. </b><fig><p>Schematic of the: (a) two-diode Dickson rectifier and (b) fabricated PCB prototype. <p></p><p>The characterization of the transformer-rectifier circuit has been carried-out in the following way. First, the PCB with the secondary winding and rectifier has been mounted on the top of another PCB where the primary winding is realized. As in the case of the transformer experiment, the two PCBs are kept in position by four plastic screws. The primary winding is then fed by an RF carrier at 868 MHz and the corresponding dc voltage is measured at the rectifier output. This experiment is repeated for several values of the available source input power and the results plotted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5705525/5705525-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 17. </b><fig><p>Output voltage versus available input power for the transformer-rectifier PCB prototype: comparison between measurements and simulations. The data have been obtained at 868 MHz. An input power of â2 dBm is needed to supply at 1.5 V the 220-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1177" role="math" style="width: 1.591em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.26em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.19em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1178"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1179"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1180"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1181"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1182"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1183" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">k</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1184" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">{\hbox{k}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> tag resistance.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5705525/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>With the above experimental setup, a 220-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1185" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1186"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1187"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1188"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1189"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1190"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1191" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">k</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1192" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">{\hbox{k}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> load is supplied at 1.5 V when a â2 dBm is applied at the input. In these conditions, the dc power is 10 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1193" role="math" style="width: 1.805em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.63em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1194"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1195" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1196"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1197"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1198"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1199"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1200" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">\mu{\hbox{W}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, this being a typical value for most RFID circuits.</p><p>At the same time, a numerical model of the whole transformer-rectifier structure has been developed. First an electromagnetic simulation of the transformer and of the microstrip line is carried out. The scattering matrix of such a circuit has then been inserted, as a black box, within a circuit simulator. Finally, the Dickson voltage multiplier has been analyzed with the harmonic balance (HB) tool.</p><p>The data obtained by the above co-simulation are reported again in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a> and they are in a very good agreement with respect to measurements. As a consequence, it is possible to conclude that the proposed coupling solution is working well and that the proposed design flow (i.e., electromagnetic simulation of the transformer and HB analysis of the rectifier) is accurate.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>This paper has shown that a small RFID Si chip and large paper substrate, UHF antennas, can be efficiently coupled by means of a heterogeneous planar transformer. Primary and secondary windings of such a transformer are implemented on the paper substrate and Si chip, respectively. As a result, the Si chip will be completely padless, while a mere placing and gluing process will be required to assembly the whole RFID tag (i.e., antenna and Si chip together). The MAG of a 1-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1201" role="math" style="width: 2.345em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.144em 1002.11em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1202"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1203"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1204"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1205"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1206"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1207"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1208" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1209"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1210"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1211" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">{\hbox {mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> heterogeneous transformer is in the order of â0.4 dB at 868 MHz, as obtained from electromagnetic simulations. In addition, such a transformer is quite tolerant to misalignments: a placing error of 150 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1212" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1213"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1214" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1215"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1216"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1217"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1218"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1219" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reduces the MAG to â0.5 dB, i.e., only 0.1 dB worse than for a perfect alignment. It is worth noticing that a similar placing error is completely unacceptable in the case of standard galvanic contacts, e.g., for 80-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1220" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1221"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1222" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1223"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1224"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1225"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1226"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1227" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> diameter pads. As a consequence, a lower cost assembly process can be used exploiting standard pick-and-place tools, the latter already available in most PCB factories.</p><p>The maximum power transfer problem has been studied proposing both optimal (simultaneous conjugate impedances) and suboptimal (pre-matched antennas with 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1228" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1229"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1230" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-106">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> input impedances) solutions. In the suboptimal case, only a simple on-chip capacitor and a proper rectifier input resistance are required. Finally, the above idea has been experimentally validated exploiting PCB prototypes. A PCB transformer (1.5-mm side) and transformer rectifier (two-diode Dickson voltage multiplier) have been fabricated and tested. The measurements confirm the feasibility of the proposed approach and the accuracy of the established design flow.</p><p>Exploiting the proposed design solution, the costs associated to the assembly of RFID tags could be reduced and novel technologies, such as paper antennas fabricated by means of ink-jet printing, enabled at market level.</p></div>

<div class="section" id="app1"><h2></h2><h1>Appendix 1 Heterogeneous Transformer Design Criteria</h1><p>The heterogeneous transformer described throughout this paper is composed by a square primary and secondary windings. height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.08em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.721em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1267"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1268"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1269" style="font-size: 70.7%; In this formalism, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1272" role="math" style="width: 2.465em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.225em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.23em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1273"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1274" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1275" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1276" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">p</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-111">i=p</script></tex-math></inline-formula> stands for primary, whereas <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1277" role="math" style="width: 2.405em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.165em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.11em 2.405em -999.997em); realized on a paper, or more in general, on a flexible substrate. A central via-hole is needed to underpass the coil and to connect one of the two antenna terminals. The minimum diameter of such a via-hole on a flexible substrate is about 150 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1356" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1357"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1358" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1359"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1360"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1361"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1362"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1363" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In addition, a pad of at least 250-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1364" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1365"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1366" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1367"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1368"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1369"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1370"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1371" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> side is required to fabricate the metallized hole. padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1402" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1404"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1405"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1406" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">p</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1407" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â¥</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1408" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">50</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1409" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã·</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1410" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">100</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1411" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1412" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1413"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1414"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1415"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1416"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1417" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">w_{p}=s_{p}\geq 50\div 100\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>The secondary winding is realized on silicon. In this case, the feature resolution is that of the adopted technology node and does not imposes serious constraints to the coil layouts. The tag, however, has a certain size (typically in the order of one square millimeter) and the secondary windings should not waste additional silicon area. A good solution for the secondary geometry is obtained by replacing the pad-ring with the coil, while keeping all the electronic inside. A third geometrical constraint is thus imposed on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1418" role="math" style="width: 1.805em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(0.904em 1001.63em 2.646em -999.997em); height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.08em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.721em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1427"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1428"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1429" style="font-size: 70.7%; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.603em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">d_{\rm out}^{(s)}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that should be less or equal to the tag side length.</p><p>As a consequence of the above considerations, we can conclude that the heterogeneous transformer has an asymmetric geometry and that, due to process resolution on paper or flexible substrates, the primary is larger than the secondary. In order to maximize the coupling coefficient, primary and secondary windings have been designed in such a way as to have the same average side length, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1432" role="math" style="width: 5.288em; In the first one, the primary winding metal track width and metal spacing has been increased from 50 to 100 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1516" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1517"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1518" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1519"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1520"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1521"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1522"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1523" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-122">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In the second one, the secondary winding metal track width has been increased from 10 to 30 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1524" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; <p></p><p>Another design criteria that has been evaluated is the number of turns of the primary coil. To study this effect, the structure of <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> has been compared with a transformer having the same secondary coil and a single-turn primary winding <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_">[3]</a>. The single-turn primary winding is designed in such a way as to have the same average side length of that with three turns, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{\rm avg}^{(p)}=750\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-133-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1703" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1704"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1705"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1706" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.306em 1000.96em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.562em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1707"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1708"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1709" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1710" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">p</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1711" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.547em 1001.14em 4.327em -999.997em); top: -3.841em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1712"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1713"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1714" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1715" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">v</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1716" style="font-size: 70.7%; The MAG of the two structures is reported in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 20</a>, and as can be seen, the transformer with the three-turn primary performs better than that with the single-turn primary. In particular, at the frequency of 868 MHz, the MAG values are of about â0.4 dB and â0.5 dB for the three- and single-turn cases, respectively. Although the single-turn primary allows for single-metal layer ink-jet printing (no via-hole), the three-turn primary can be more easily matched to its optimum source impedance, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 21</a>.

<div class="section" id="app2"><h2></h2><h1>Appendix 2 Transformer Equivalent-Circuit Extraction</h1><p>The transformer equivalent circuit has been extracted from the electromagnetic simulations with the following procedure. First the computed scattering parameters of the structure are converted into impedance parameters. Primary and secondary inductances are evaluated with <disp-formula id="deqn7-8" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{L_{1}(f)=&amp;\,{\Im\{Z_{11}\}\over 2\pi f}&amp;\hbox{(7)}\cr L_{2}(f)=&amp;\,{\Im\{Z_{22}\}\over 2\pi f}&amp;\hbox{(8)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-136-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1752" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; <script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

Such a method exploits a magnetic coupling mechanism, thus not requiring for galvanic contacts between the Si chip and antenna itself. The magnetic coupling is established by a planar transformer, the primary and secondary windings of which are implemented on flexible substrate and Si chip, respectively. As a result, the Si chip can be assembled on the antenna with a mere placing and gluing process. First, the idea has been validated by theory. Electromagnetic simulations of a square heterogeneous transformer (1.0-mm side) show a maximum available power gain (MAG) of -0.4 dB at 868 MHz. In addition, the heterogeneous transformer is also quite tolerant with respect to misalignment between primary and secondary. An offset error of 150 &amp;#x03BC;m reduces the MAG to - 0.5 dB. A sub-optimal matching strategy, exploiting a simple on-chip capacitor, is then developed for antennas with 50- &amp;#x03A9; input impedances. Finally, the idea has been experimentally validated exploiting printed circuit board (PCB) prototypes. A PCB transformer (1.5-mm side) and a transformer rectifier (two-diode Dickson multiplier) have been fabricated and tested. Measurements indicates a MAG of -0.3 dB at 868 MHz for the transformer and the capability of the developed rectifier to supply a 220-k&amp;#x03A9; load at 1.5 V with a - 2-dBm input
